## Assistant Responses

[01:12:54] Here's the **best integrated configuration** for your setup:

[01:13:02] **Done.** Edwin is now configured for integrated Shad context. Here's what we set up:

## Your Integrated System

```
You ask me something
       ↓
Edwin receives your message
       ↓
shad-context plugin kicks in (autoRecall: true)
       ↓
Shad searches your vaults (Hodos + workspace)
       ↓
Relevant context injected into my prompt
       ↓
I answer with actual knowledge from your codebase
```

## What's Configured

| Setting | Value | Effect |
|---------|-------|--------|
| `vaultPaths` | Hodos + workspace | I can search both your codebase and my memory |
| `searchMode` | hybrid | BM25 + vector search for best results |
| `autoRecall` | true | Context auto-fetched before every response |
| `autoCapture` | true | Conversations get saved back to vault |
| `leafModel` | haiku | Fast, cheap synthesis for context briefs |

## What Happens Now

1. **Gateway is restarting** with new config
2. **Every message** will now auto-fetch relevant context from your vaults
3. Ask me about Hodos co

[01:15:13] **Yes, exactly.** 

When you run `edwin gateway`, it will:
1. Load the config we just set (with `shad-context` plugin enabled)
2. Automatically call Shad for context retrieval on every message
3. Search your Hodos + workspace vaults before answering

**Optional enhancement:** For faster repeated queries, you can also run the Shad server in a separate terminal:
```bash
shad server start
```
This adds Redis caching, but it's not required — Shad CLI works without it.

**TL;DR:** Your command is correct. Start Edwin, and Shad integration is automatic.

## What's Configured

| Setting | Value | Effect |
|---------|-------|--------|
| `vaultPaths` | Hodos + workspace | I can search both your codebase and my memory |
| `searchMode` | hybrid | BM25 + vector search for best results |
| `autoRecall` | true | Context auto-fetched before every response |
| `autoCapture` | true | Conversations get saved back to vault |
| `leafModel` | haiku | Fast, cheap synthesis for context briefs |

[01:15:13] **Yes, exactly.** 

When you run `edwin gateway`, it will:
1. Load the config we just set (with `shad-context` plugin enabled)

```bash
shad server start
```
This adds Redis caching, but it's not required — Shad CLI works without it.

---

## Multi-Agent

**What it is:** Running separate "brains" with isolated context/memory.

**Example use cases:**
- A "Hodos Dev" agent that only knows Hodos code
- A "Marketing" agent with a different personality for content
- Separate agents for different clients/projects

**When to set it up:** When you find yourself context-switching constantly and want true isolation. You're fine with one agent for now.

---

## Skills

**What they are:** Packaged instructions that teach me how to do specific things.

**You already have:**
- `coding-agent` — run coding agents (Codex, Claude Code, etc.) via background processes
- `weather` — get forecasts
- `

[01:37:50] ## What I Recommend Setting Up

**Now:** Nothing more — you're ready to work. We did the heavy lifting (QMD, Shad, shad-context plugin).

**Later (when needed):**
- **Channels** — if you want to reach me via WhatsApp/Telegram/Discord
- **Cron jobs** — for scheduled reminders or automated checks
- **Nodes** — if you want Edwin on your phone

---

## Multi-Agent

**What it is:** Running separate "brains" with isolated context/memory.

**Example use cases:**
- A "Hodos Dev" agent that only knows Hodos code
- A "Marketing" agent with a different personality for content
- Separate agents for different clients/projects

**When to set it up:** When you find yourself context-switching constantly and want true isolation. You're fine with one agent for now.

---

## Skills

**What they are:** Packaged instructions that teach me how to do specific things.

**You already have:**
- `coding-agent` — run coding agents (Codex, Claude Code, etc.) via background processes
- `weather` — get forecasts
- `

[01:41:25] **Honest answer:** Sort of, but with constraints.

## What Works

| Approach | How it works | Limitations |
|----------|--------------|-------------|
| **Sub-agents** | I spawn background agents that work independently and report back | Each has a ~10 min timeout by default |
| **Cron jobs** | Schedule tasks to run at specific times | Each run is independent (no continuous work) |
| **Write to disk** | Sub-agents save findings to files you read in the morning | Works well for research output |

## What Doesn't Work

- I can't literally run for 8 hours straight — sessions have timeouts
- I don't "stay awake" between interactions — I wake up when pinged

## What I'd Recommend for Tonight

1. Wallet security review
2. Authentication flow review
3. Process isolation analysis
4. BSV protocol compliance check
5. Best practices research (BRC standards)
6. etc.

## The Sessions Folder

[02:06:53] That's from Shad's **autoCapture** feature — it saves our conversation summaries to your vault so future sessions can recall what we discussed. You didn't create it; the system did.

---

## How to "Train" Me

**You don't train me in the traditional sense.** I wake up fresh every session. Instead:

| What works | What doesn't |
|------------|--------------|
| Building searchable docs (Shad/QMD can retrieve them) | Telling me things once and expecting me to remember |
| Writing to `memory/*.md` files | Relying on conversation history |
| Creating context files in the codebase | Assuming I learned from past sessions |

**The pattern:**
```
You teach me something
    ↓
I write it to a file (memory/ or codebase docs)
    ↓
Shad indexes it
    ↓
Next session, I retrieve it when relevant
```

---

## What the Overnight Task Should Be

**Not for me to review code.** That's backwards.

**For me to BUILD REFERENCE DOCS that I can retrieve later.**

The goal is:
1. I read the codebase deeply
2.

## How to "Train" Me

**You don't train me in the traditional sense.** I wake up fresh every session. Instead:

| What works | What doesn't |

    ↓
Shad indexes it
    ↓
Next session, I retrieve it when relevant
```

## Sprint 9: Settings Persistence + Profile Import

**What it involves:**
1. **Settings persistence** — JSON file (`settings.json`) + C++ `SettingsManager` singleton
2. **Profile import** — Read Chrome/Brave/Edge bookmarks (JSON) and history (SQLite)

**Research needed:**
- Chrome's `Bookmarks` JSON format (documented, straightforward)
- Chrome's `History` SQLite schema (need to verify)
- File locking behavior (Chrome locks files while running)
- Cross-platform paths (Windows vs macOS)

## Assistant Responses

[02:28:27] Good question. Let me clarify the distinction:

**CLAUDE.md / CONTEXT.md** = Project documentation *in the repo* for any AI coding assistant (Claude Code, Cursor, Copilot, me via Edwin). Tells the AI about the codebase structure, conventions, current work.

**Edwin** = The *infrastructure* that runs me. It's a gateway/daemon that provides:

| Capability | What it does |
|------------|--------------|
| **Multi-channel** | Reach you on webchat, Signal, Telegram, Discord, etc. |
| **Persistent memory** | Workspace files survive sessions (SOUL.md, memory/, tasks/) |
| **QMD + Shad** | Semantic search across vaults (we just set this up) |
| **Cron/reminders** | Schedule tasks, wake me up at specific times |
| **Skills** | Modular capabilities (weather, tmux, coding-agent, etc.) |
| **Tool execution** | Run commands, browser automation, file ops |

**What we've set up so far:**
- ✅ QMD indexing workspace + Hodos (242 files, 1109 chunks)
- ✅ Shad for semantic recall
- ✅ Memory files for sessi

## Research Complete — Summary

### Key Finding: Two Concepts

| Concept | What It Is | Our Responsibility |
|---------|------------|-------------------|
| **Browser Profile** | Local data container (bookmarks, history, cookies) | ✅ Yes — Sprint 9d |
| **Browser Account Sync** | Cloud sync (Google, Firefox Account, etc.) | ❌ No — not MVP |

**Website logins (x.com, YouTube, Gmail) are just cookies stored per-profile.** Users log into websites normally — we don't need to build OAuth flows or Google integration.

### How the Big 4 Do It

| Browser | Profile Picker | Header Indicator | Multi-Instance |
|---------|---------------|------------------|----------------|
| **Chrome** | Optional at startup | Avatar + name + color | Different profiles = different windows |
| **Firefox** | Via about:profiles | Profile name in window | Same as Chrome |
| **Safari** | No (toolbar button) | Name + symbol + color in toolbar | Same as Chrome |
| **Edge** | Optional at startup | Avatar | Same as Ch

## Found the Issue: Scriptlet Injection

I see **7178 chars of scriptlets being injected into x.com**:

```
[06:55:54] 💉 Injecting scriptlets for https://x.com/ (7178 chars)
[06:56:00] 🎨 Cosmetic P1: css=17 script=7178 generichide=1 url=https://x.com/login
[06:56:00] 💉 Injecting scriptlets for https://x.com/login (7178 chars)
```

The adblock scriptlets override browser APIs (`fetch`, `XHR`, `JSON.parse`) to block ads. These scriptlets work great for YouTube but may be breaking x.com's login flow.

### Quick Test

**Can you try disabling the Privacy Shield for x.com?**

1. Click the shield icon in the header
2. Toggle OFF the shield for x.com
3. Reload the page
4. Try the login button again

If the login form appears with shield disabled, we know the scriptlets are the issue.

### If That's the Problem

We have a few options:
1. **Whitelist x.com** from scriptlet injection (keep network-level ad blocking, disable JS overrides)
2. **More granular scriptlets** - some sites need e

Let me check the logs for that login error:

[14:30:05] No browser-side errors in the logs. That `g;176951960484509424...` error is **from x.com's servers**, not us.

## What's Happening

X.com is rejecting the login attempt. This is likely:
1. **Wrong email** — you don't remember which email you used
2. **Bot/fingerprint detection** — x.com is aggressive about detecting "unusual" browsers
3. **Rate limiting** — too many attempts

## Quickest Path Forward

**Option A: Check your x.com account in the other browser**
1. Open x.com in Chrome where you're already logged in
2. Go to Settings → Your Account → Account Information
3. See which email is associated

**Option B: Try "Sign in with Google"**
- If you set it up with Google SSO, this should work
- Google will send you an approval on your phone/other device

**Option C: Do Sprint 9 first (my recommendation)**
- Import your Chrome profile that has x.com already logged in
- The session cookies transfer
- You're logged in immediately without entering credentials
- **This actually validates Sp

[14:30:05] No browser-side errors in the logs. That `g;176951960484509424...` error is **from x.com's servers**, not us.

## What's Happening

X.com is rejecting the login attempt. This is likely:
1. **Wrong email** — you don't remember which email you used
2. **Bot/fingerprint detection** — x.com is aggressive about detecting "unusual" browsers
3. **Rate limiting** — too many attempts

## Quickest Path Forward

**Option A: Check your x.com account in the other browser**
1. Open x.com in Chrome where you're already logged in
2. Go to Settings → Your Account → Account Information
3. See which email is associated

**Option B: Try "Sign in with Google"**
- If you set it up with Google SSO, this should work
- Google will send you an approval on your phone/other device

**Option C: Do Sprint 9 first (my recommendation)**
- Import your Chrome profile that has x.com already logged in
- The session cookies transfer
- You're logged in immediately without entering credentials
- **This actually validates Sp

[14:36:05] X.com's login is finicky — usernames often don't work in the login flow even though they work elsewhere. The login form typically wants:
- **Email** (you don't have one associated)
- **Phone number** ✓ (you have this)
- **Google SSO** (might be linked via your Android)

## Try This Order

1. **Phone number first** — Enter your phone number in the login field (with country code, like +1XXXXXXXXXX). X.com will text you a code.

2. **If that fails, try Google sign-in** — Since your Android/phone is tied to Google, and x.com might have linked via that.

## Why Username Doesn't Work

X.com's login flow changed a while back. The "username" field in login actually expects:
- Email address
- Phone number
- NOT your @handle

The @handle is for display/mentions, not authentication. Annoying but that's how they built it.

---

**Try the phone number.** If that works, you're in and we've validated that Hodos can handle x.com auth (with shield off). Then we can move to Sprint 9 knowing the core bro

| Action | When | Why |
|--------|------|-----|

```
1. [30 min] Add hardcoded scriptlet whitelist for auth-critical sites
   → x.com, twitter.com, google.com, accounts.google.com, login.microsoftonline.com

   → Test x.co

## Assistant Responses

[17:24:06] No WAL files — Chrome is using journal mode, not WAL. The fix won't help here. But the COUNT worked (4189), so the database IS readable.

Let me add more debugging to see exactly what's happening in the query:

[17:24:26] Rebuild and test again:

```powershell
cmake --build build --config Release
```

Then run the import — this will tell us if the `urls` table has data when accessed during import.

[17:29:05] Web search isn't configured. But let me think through this:

**Possible causes:**

1. **Database state differs between detection and import** — Detection runs when Settings opens, import runs later. Chrome might checkpoint the journal between these times.

2. **Copy timing issue** — Chrome might be mid-write during import, causing a corrupt copy.

3. **Database encryption** — Some Chrome versions encrypt databases (but COUNT worked, so probably not).

4. **Schema version** — Chrome 120+ changed some History schema, but `urls` table should still exist.

**Most likely culprit:** The detection (which worked) and import (which failed) happen at different moments. Chrome's state was different.

**Alternative approach to try if debugging doesn't reveal the issue:** Close Chrome completely before importing, then test.

Let me know what the new debug logs show — specifically the "Total rows in urls table" and "Sample URL" lines.

[17:30:50] You're absolutely right — that's a gap in my setup. Let's fix it now:

[17:31:12] The configure wizard is interactive — you'll need to run it. Here's what to do:

**1. Get a Brave Search API key** (free tier: 2000 queries/month):
- Go to https://brave.com/search/api/
- Sign up / sign in
- Create an API key

**2. Run the configure wizard:**
```powershell
edwin configure --section web
```

Or manually add to your Edwin config (`~/.edwin/config.yaml` or via Gateway):
```yaml
web:
  braveApiKey: "your-key-here"
```

**3. Restart Edwin Gateway** for the change to take effect.

Once that's set up, I can do web searches for debugging issues like this Chrome SQLite problem.

## Assistant Responses

[17:30:50] You're absolutely right — that's a gap in my setup. Let's fix it now:

[17:31:12] The configure wizard is interactive — you'll need to run it. Here's what to do:

**1. Get a Brave Search API key** (free tier: 2000 queries/month):
- Go to https://brave.com/search/api/
- Sign up / sign in
- Create an API key

**2. Run the configure wizard:**
```powershell
edwin configure --section web
```

Or manually add to your Edwin config (`~/.edwin/config.yaml` or via Gateway):
```yaml
web:
  braveApiKey: "your-key-here"
```

**3. Restart Edwin Gateway** for the change to take effect.

Once that's set up, I can do web searches for debugging issues like this Chrome SQLite problem.

[17:31:12] The configure wizard is interactive — you'll need to run it. Here's what to do:

**1. Get a Brave Search API key** (free tier: 2000 queries/month):
- Go to https://brave.com/search/api/

edwin configure --section web
```

```yaml
web:
  braveApiKey: "your-key-here"
```

[17:31:30] HEARTBEAT_OK

[18:09:01] **Quick answers:**

1. **Brave API key = Brave Search engine** (not Brave browser). Required regardless of which browser you use.

2. **Edwin's search flow:**
   - `web_search` tool → Brave Search API → returns results
   - Claude doesn't search — Edwin does, then feeds me the results
   - Your Claude subscription pays for *me thinking*, Brave API pays for *web searches*

3. **Best config:** Brave Search API (free tier = 2000 searches/month, plenty for most use)

**Setup:**
```
1. https://brave.com/search/api/ → get free API key
2. Add to Edwin config: web.braveApiKey = "your-key"
3. Restart gateway
```

That's it. No other search options currently in Edwin.

[17:31:30] HEARTBEAT_OK

[18:09:01] **Quick answers:**

1. **Brave API key = Brave Search engine** (not Brave browser). Required regardless of which browser you use.

2. **Edwin's search flow:**
   - `web_search` tool → Brave Search API → returns results
   - Claude doesn't search — Edwin does, then feeds me the results
   - Your Claude subscription pays for *me thinking*, Brave API pays for *web searches*

3. **Best config:** Brave Search API (free tier = 2000 searches/month, plenty for most use)

**Setup:**
```
1. https://brave.com/search/api/ → get free API key
2. Add to Edwin config: web.braveApiKey = "your-key"
3. Restart gateway
```

That's it. No other search options currently in Edwin.

[18:16:12] You're right — Brave may have removed/hidden the free tier. Currently **Brave Search API is Edwin's only web search option**.

**Brave pricing:** Starts at $5/month for 2000 queries (or $0.003/query pay-as-you-go).

**Alternatives that would require Edwin changes:**
- SerpAPI (Google results, has free tier)
- Tavily (AI-focused, has free tier)
- DuckDuckGo (no official API but scrapeable)

**My recommendation:** 
- $5/month for Brave is reasonable for dev work
- Or skip it for now — I can work without web search, just less efficiently for debugging obscure issues

Your call. Want to proceed without it and get back to the import debugging?

[18:24:33] Noted in memory. That's an important "why" for everything we're building.

**Your questions:**

**"AI-focused" (Tavily):** Designed for AI agents — returns cleaner, pre-summarized results optimized for LLM consumption. Less noise than raw Google results. Yes, potentially better fit for Edwin.

**"Edwin changes":** I need to check if it's just config or actual code changes:

[18:24:53] **Good news — Edwin already supports two providers (no code changes needed):**

| Provider | API Key | Pricing |
|----------|---------|---------|
| **Brave** (default) | `BRAVE_API_KEY` | $5/mo subscription |
| **Perplexity** | `PERPLEXITY_API_KEY` or `OPENROUTER_API_KEY` | Pay-per-query |

**OpenRouter is pay-per-use** — no subscription! You load credits and pay per query. This aligns with your mission.

**To switch to Perplexity via OpenRouter:**

1. Go to https://openrouter.ai — create account, add credits ($5-10 to start)
2. Get API key
3. Set in Edwin config:
```yaml
tools:
  web:
    search:
      provider: perplexity
```
4. Set env var: `OPENROUTER_API_KEY=your-key`
5. Restart gateway

**"AI-focused" means:** Perplexity returns synthesized answers with citations, not just raw links. Better for agents.

Want to try OpenRouter? It's pay-as-you-go — exactly what you're building toward.

## Assistant Responses

[18:24:53] **Good news — Edwin already supports two providers (no code changes needed):**

| Provider | API Key | Pricing |
|----------|---------|---------|
| **Brave** (default) | `BRAVE_API_KEY` | $5/mo subscription |
| **Perplexity** | `PERPLEXITY_API_KEY` or `OPENROUTER_API_KEY` | Pay-per-query |

**OpenRouter is pay-per-use** — no subscription! You load credits and pay per query. This aligns with your mission.

**To switch to Perplexity via OpenRouter:**

1. Go to https://openrouter.ai — create account, add credits ($5-10 to start)
2. Get API key
3. Set in Edwin config:
```yaml
tools:
  web:
    search:
      provider: perplexity
```
4. Set env var: `OPENROUTER_API_KEY=your-key`
5. Restart gateway

**"AI-focused" means:** Perplexity returns synthesized answers with citations, not just raw links. Better for agents.

Want to try OpenRouter? It's pay-as-you-go — exactly what you're building toward.

[18:31:29] HEARTBEAT_OK

[18:33:44] You're right to push back. Let me think about what you already have:

**What your existing accounts provide:**
- Claude subscription → pays for *me thinking* (via Anthropic API)
- Claude.ai web interface has search, but **no API access** to it
- ChatGPT has browsing, but **no API access** to it

**Options without new accounts:**

1. **Use `web_fetch` instead** — I can fetch any URL you give me, I just can't *find* the URL myself. You search, I read.

2. **Browser tool** — Edwin can control a browser. I could literally Google things through browser automation:
```
browser → open google.com → type query → read results
```
Clunky but works with zero new accounts.

3. **You search, paste to me** — Low-tech but effective.

**The real answer:** Your Claude subscription *should* include search for programmatic use, but Anthropic doesn't expose it via API. That's the gap.

Want me to try option 2 (browser automation for searches)? It's slower but uses what you already have.

[18:35:17] Yes, I have a few options:

1. **Browser tool** — If you log into Claude.ai in a browser, I can control it (click, type, read). You'd attach the tab via Edwin's browser relay.

2. **Tmux skill** — I can send keystrokes to a terminal session and read output. If you have Claude CLI or similar running in tmux, I can interact with it.

3. **Exec with PTY** — I can run interactive terminal commands directly.

**The workflow would be:**
- You log in once (browser or CLI)
- I send queries through that session
- Read results back

**Practical question:** Which Claude interface are you thinking?
- **Claude.ai web** → I'd use browser tool
- **Claude CLI** (if you have it) → I'd use tmux/exec

It's a bit meta (Claude controlling Claude), but it would use your existing subscription for searches. Want to try it?

## Assistant Responses

[18:33:44] You're right to push back. Let me think about what you already have:

**What your existing accounts provide:**
- Claude subscription → pays for *me thinking* (via Anthropic API)
- Claude.ai web interface has search, but **no API access** to it
- ChatGPT has browsing, but **no API access** to it

**Options without new accounts:**

1. **Use `web_fetch` instead** — I can fetch any URL you give me, I just can't *find* the URL myself. You search, I read.

2. **Browser tool** — Edwin can control a browser. I could literally Google things through browser automation:
```
browser → open google.com → type query → read results
```
Clunky but works with zero new accounts.

3. **You search, paste to me** — Low-tech but effective.

**The real answer:** Your Claude subscription *should* include search for programmatic use, but Anthropic doesn't expose it via API. That's the gap.

Want me to try option 2 (browser automation for searches)? It's slower but uses what you already have.

[18:35:17] Yes, I have a few options:

1. **Browser tool** — If you log into Claude.ai in a browser, I can control it (click, type, read). You'd attach the tab via Edwin's browser relay.

2. **Tmux skill** — I can send keystrokes to a terminal session and read output. If you have Claude CLI or similar running in tmux, I can interact with it.

3. **Exec with PTY** — I can run interactive terminal commands directly.

**The workflow would be:**
- You log in once (browser or CLI)
- I send queries through that session
- Read results back

**Practical question:** Which Claude interface are you thinking?
- **Claude.ai web** → I'd use browser tool
- **Claude CLI** (if you have it) → I'd use tmux/exec

It's a bit meta (Claude controlling Claude), but it would use your existing subscription for searches. Want to try it?

[18:39:25] Sounds good. Once you have the API key:

**Option A: Environment variable (quick)**
```powershell
$env:PERPLEXITY_API_KEY = "pplx-your-key-here"
```
Then restart Edwin gateway.

**Option B: Edwin config (persistent)**
```yaml
tools:
  web:
    search:
      provider: perplexity
      perplexity:
        apiKey: "pplx-your-key-here"
```

Let me know when it's set up — I'll test it with a search for the Chrome SQLite issue we were debugging.

## Assistant Responses

[18:48:54] 🎉 **Web search is working!**

And look — it found our exact issue! Key insight:

> **Wrong tables or missing JOINs**: History data splits across tables like `visits` (visit details) and `urls` (URLs). Simple `SELECT * FROM visits` may appear empty without joining

**The fix:** We're querying `urls` table directly, but Chrome separates data:
- `urls` table = unique URLs
- `visits` table = actual visit records

We need to JOIN them, or the `urls` table might be empty/stale while `visits` has the data.

Let me update our import query:

[18:49:01] Wait — actually our COUNT query (`SELECT COUNT(*) FROM urls`) returned 4189, so `urls` table HAS data. The mystery is why SELECT returns 0 rows when COUNT returns 4189.

Let me check if Matt ran the import with the new diagnostic logging:

[18:49:18] The debug log isn't there — Hodos isn't running. 

**Summary of where we are:**

1. ✅ Web search configured and working
2. 🔄 History import still needs debugging

**Next step:** Run Hodos again, open Settings → Import tab, click "Import All" on Chrome. Then I'll check the new diagnostic logs which should show:
- `Total rows in urls table: X`
- `Sample URL: ...`
- `Simple query returned: X rows`

This will tell us exactly what's happening inside the import function.

## Assistant Responses

[19:43:25] Great feedback! Let me address everything:

## Current Status

**Working well:**
- ✅ History individual delete (immediate update)
- ✅ History clear all (the refresh might've been a race condition - I'll check)
- ✅ Cookies individual delete

**Bug found:**
- 🐛 "Delete selected" button exists but no checkbox selection mechanism - that's incomplete UI

## Your Questions

**Cache vs cookies testing:** Test cache clear first - it's simpler and less disruptive than nuking all cookies.

**Does import bring in cookies?** No, and intentionally so:
- Cookies are session-tied and often expire within hours/days
- They're tied to authentication tokens that may be invalidated
- Importing them would be a security concern (copying auth state)
- Chrome/Brave/Edge don't import cookies either for these reasons

**What CAN be imported:**
- ✅ Bookmarks (working)
- ✅ History (fixing now)
- ⚠️ Passwords - *technically possible* but complex (Chrome encrypts with Windows DPAPI, tied to user account)
- ⚠️ Cred

## Changes Made

### 1. SQL Query Fix (unique URLs only)
**File:** `cef-native/src/core/HistoryManager.cpp`

- `GetHistory()` - Now queries `urls` table directly instead of JOIN with `visits`
- `SearchHistory()` - Same fix

**Before:** Returned one row per visit (5 visits = 5 rows for same URL)
**After:** Returns one row per URL with `visit_count` showing total visits

**Files:** `HistoryManager.h` and `HistoryManager.cpp`

Added 2-second debounce to prevent duplicate logging from multiple CEF events:
- If same URL is visited within 2 seconds, skip logging
- Uses `std::unordered_map` with automatic cleanup

[20:19:08] Love that idea - **launching a new instance is exactly what Chrome does**, and it's great UX:

## Chrome's Approach (Recommended)

1. User clicks profile avatar → dropdown shows profiles
2. User selects "Work" profile → **new window opens** with Work profile
3. Original window stays open (user can close it or keep both)

**Why this is better:**
- No jarring close/reopen experience
- User can have multiple profiles open simultaneously
- Can drag tabs or copy between profile windows
- Each window is clearly "this is my Work browser / Personal browser"
- If one crashes, the other survives

## Implementation

```
HodosBrowserShell.exe --profile="Work"
```

Each instance:
- Reads `--profile` argument (defaults to "Default")
- Loads data from `%APPDATA%/HodosBrowser/<profile_name>/`
- Shows profile avatar with that profile's color/initial

**Profile dropdown options:**
- Current profile (shown with checkmark)
- Other profiles (click = launch new instance)
- "Add profile" → opens profile crea

[20:32:02] Good catch! That's a **warning** (not an error) — build succeeded ✅

## The Warning

It's in `ProfileManager::ParseProfileArgument` line 384 where I convert `wstring` to `string`:

```cpp
return std::string(profileW.begin(), profileW.end());  // ⚠️ wchar_t → char
```

This works fine for ASCII profile names ("Default", "Work") but would mangle Unicode characters (e.g., "工作" for "Work" in Chinese).

## Quick Fix

[20:32:19] **Fixed!** Uses proper `WideCharToMultiByte` conversion now.

But your **current build is fine for testing** — the warning only affects non-ASCII profile names. Go ahead and test with the build you have.

If you want a clean build later:
```powershell
cmake --build build --config Release
```

What are you seeing in the browser? 🔍

[20:48:13] **Full path:**
```
C:\Users\archb\AppData\Roaming\HodosBrowser\profiles.json
```

---

**Important clarification:** Hodos profiles are **NOT Google accounts!**

They're **local browser profiles** — like Chrome's profile system but without any cloud sync:

| Hodos Profile | Google Account |
|---------------|----------------|
| Local data separation | Cloud sync |
| No login required | Requires Google login |
| Separate cookies per profile | Tied to Google identity |
| Separate history/bookmarks | Synced to Google servers |

**What profiles give you:**
- "Work" profile → logged into work Gmail, Slack, etc.
- "Personal" profile → logged into personal YouTube, Twitter, etc.
- Each profile is isolated — different cookies, different sessions

**No Google prompts** — you create a profile locally, then manually log into whatever sites you want in each profile.

---

Building the dropdown now:

[20:49:27] **Done!** ✅ TypeScript compiles.

## Profile Dropdown Added

**What you'll see:**
1. Profile button now shows a **colored avatar** with initial (instead of generic icon)
2. Click it → **dropdown menu** appears
3. Shows all profiles with checkmark on current one
4. Click another profile → **launches new browser window** with that profile
5. "Add profile" → type name, press Enter → creates profile (random color)

## To Test

Frontend should hot-reload. If not:
```powershell
cd frontend
npm run dev
```

**Test steps:**
1. Click profile avatar (should show "D" for Default)
2. Click "Add profile"
3. Type "Work" and press Enter
4. See "Work" appear in the list
5. Click "Work" → **new browser window should open**
6. Check `profiles.json` — should now have 2 profiles

---

**Note:** When you click a different profile, it launches `HodosBrowserShell.exe --profile="Work"` as a new process. The new window will have its own cookies, history, etc.

[20:50:24] Great question - let me clarify because these are **two separate issues**:

## The x.com Problem (Sprint 10)
**Root cause:** Our adblock scriptlets break x.com's authentication JavaScript.
**Fix needed:** Scriptlet compatibility system (like Brave) that disables problematic scriptlets on certain sites.
**Status:** NOT STARTED - we planned it but pivoted to Sprint 9.

## Multi-Profile (Sprint 9d - what we just built)
**Purpose:** Data separation - "Work" profile has work logins, "Personal" has personal logins.
**What it does:** Each profile stores its own cookies (including logins), history, bookmarks.
**Does NOT fix:** The x.com scriptlet problem. If x.com is broken in Default profile, it's broken in Work profile too.

---

## Are we off track?

Looking back at our sprint index:
- Sprint 9: Settings/Import/Profiles ← we're finishing this
- **Sprint 10: Scriptlet Compatibility** ← this fixes x.com
- Sprint 11: Menu UX
- Sprint 12: Cookie/Fingerprint

**You're right to ask.** If x.com (a

## Assistant Responses

[20:57:07] You're absolutely right - I'm sorry. I keep making this mistake.

## The Fix

Profile menu needs to be an **overlay** like Wallet/Settings/Cookies panels, not inline React in header_hwnd.

## How to Prevent This (Edwin Memory)

This is **exactly** what Edwin's workspace is for! We should document this in the Hodos project's `CLAUDE.md`:

[20:57:36] **Added to CLAUDE.md** - this will be read every time I work on Hodos.

Now let me **revert the inline menu** and make it trigger an overlay properly:

[20:58:22] **Reverted.** Now it's just a button that will trigger `profile_panel_show`.

## To Answer Your Question

**Yes, this IS what Edwin is designed to do.** The `CLAUDE.md` file in each project is loaded every time I work on it. I just added the UI architecture rules there.

**What can be saved:**

| File | Purpose | Example |
|------|---------|---------|
| `CLAUDE.md` | Project rules, architecture, patterns | "All panels must be overlays" |
| `development-docs/*.md` | Technical decisions, sprint plans | Sprint docs |
| `working-notes.md` | Ongoing decisions, learnings | What we discover during dev |

**The CLAUDE.md I just updated now says:**
> ⚠️ CRITICAL: UI Architecture Rules
> NEVER add new panels/menus/dropdowns directly to MainBrowserView.tsx (header_hwnd)
> All UI panels MUST be implemented as overlays...

This will be in my context every time I touch Hodos.

## To Answer Your Question

**Yes, this IS what Edwin is designed to do.** The `CLAUDE.md` file in each project is loaded every time I work on it. I just added the UI architecture rules there.

**What can be saved:**

| File | Purpose | Example |
|------|---------|---------|
| `CLAUDE.md` | Project rules, architecture, patterns | "All panels must be overlays" |
| `development-docs/*.md` | Technical decisions, sprint plans | Sprint docs |
| `working-notes.md` | Ongoing decisions, learnings | What we discover during dev |

**The CLAUDE.md I just updated now says:**
> ⚠️ CRITICAL: UI Architecture Rules
> NEVER add new panels/menus/dropdowns directly to MainBrowserView.tsx (header_hwnd)
> All UI panels MUST be implemented as overlays...

This will be in my context every time I touch Hodos.

## Assistant Responses

[21:34:00] Found it! The profile panel overlay:
1. **Doesn't get CEF focus** when shown - need to call `SetFocus(true)` on the browser
2. **Is too small** - 260x350, needs to be bigger

Let me fix both issues:

[21:35:28] Now let me also add the CEF focus pattern to the documentation:

[21:35:36] Fixed both issues:

**1. Overlay Size** (260x350 → 380x500):
- Width increased for profile list + create form
- Height increased for avatar picker + color grid + buttons
- Added screen clamping with 20px margin

**2. Text Input Focus** (CEF windowless quirk):
- Removed `SWP_NOACTIVATE` flag so Windows allows focus
- Added `SetForegroundWindow()` + `SetFocus()` on the HWND
- Added `browser->GetHost()->SetFocus(true)` + Invalidate when showing
- Already had focus in `OnAfterCreated`, but re-showing overlay needs it again

**Root cause**: CEF windowless rendering requires explicit focus management at both Windows HWND level AND CEF browser level. Other overlays that work (like Settings) have this pattern in their `OnAfterCreated`.

## Assistant Responses

[21:46:07] **Found the root cause!**

Profile panel WndProc is missing critical keyboard handling that wallet has:

| Feature | Wallet | Profile Panel |
|---------|--------|---------------|
| WM_MOUSEACTIVATE | `MA_ACTIVATE` | `MA_NOACTIVATE` ❌ |
| WM_LBUTTONDOWN | `SetFocus(hwnd)` + forward | Just forward ❌ |
| WM_KEYDOWN | Handles + forwards to CEF | **MISSING** ❌ |
| WM_CHAR | Handles + forwards to CEF | **MISSING** ❌ |

Let me fix the profile panel WndProc:

[21:46:35] Now let me update the documentation with this critical pattern:

[21:46:46] **Root cause found!** The profile panel WndProc was missing keyboard event forwarding.

**Fixed:**

1. **WM_MOUSEACTIVATE**: Changed from `MA_NOACTIVATE` to `MA_ACTIVATE`
2. **WM_LBUTTONDOWN**: Added `SetFocus(hwnd)` + CEF `SetFocus(true)`
3. **WM_KEYDOWN/WM_KEYUP/WM_CHAR**: Added all keyboard event forwarding to CEF (was completely missing!)
4. **WM_RBUTTONDOWN**: Added for completeness
5. **Browser settings**: Added `javascript_access_clipboard` and `javascript_dom_paste`
6. **HWND style**: Added `WS_VISIBLE` flag

The wallet overlay WndProc has ~150 lines of keyboard handling that the profile panel was missing entirely. Without forwarding WM_CHAR events to CEF, typing simply does nothing.

Rebuild:
```powershell
cd C:\Users\archb\Hodos-Browser\cef-native\build
cmake --build . --config Release
```

## Assistant Responses

[22:11:30] Found the relevant section (#9). Now let me research best practices:

[22:13:06] Good research gathered. Let me synthesize this into a comprehensive recommendation:

[22:14:30] Created comprehensive analysis at `development-docs/browser-core/multi-instance-profile-testing.md`.

## Summary

### Your Observation is Correct
In dev mode, clicking a profile opens a new CEF window that connects to the same `localhost:5137` dev server. This works but doesn't test production behavior where each process would load bundled files.

### Key Recommendations

**1. Add "Stage Mode" for Testing**
```powershell
# Build frontend to static files
cd frontend && npm run build

# Run CEF in bundled mode (not dev server)
$env:HODOS_USE_BUNDLED = "1"
./HodosBrowserShell.exe --profile="Default"
```
This simulates production without needing a full installer.

**2. Profile Switching (Current Behavior is Correct!)**
Launching new process with `--profile="Name"` is exactly what Chrome does. Each profile = separate process for security isolation.

**3. Startup Profile Picker**
| Profiles | Behavior |
|----------|----------|
| 0 or 1 | Auto-load, no picker |
| 2+ | Show full-screen picker

## Summary

### Sprint 10 (Scriptlet Compatibility) ⭐⭐⭐⭐⭐
**Excellent** — Architecture matches Brave exactly:
- `brave-unbreak.txt` → `hodos-unbreak.txt` ✅
- `#@#+js()` syntax is correct approach ✅
- Per-site toggle gives users more control than Brave

**⚠️ Critical check before starting**: Write unit test to verify `#@#+js()` works in adblock-rust 0.10.3. If it doesn't, you'll need C++ bypass logic instead.

### Sprint 11 (Menu + Settings) ⭐⭐⭐⭐
**Good, but scope risk** — 18+ hours estimated, likely 24-30 actual.

**Recommendation**: Split into:
- 11a: Menu + 4 critical settings sections (General, Privacy, Downloads, About)
- 11b: Remaining sections + wire settings to behavior + retire overlay

### Sprint 12 (Cookie + Fingerprint) ⭐⭐⭐⭐⭐
**Excellent** — Fingerprinting approach matches Brave's farbling system exactly:
- Session seed → HMAC per domain ✅
- Canvas/WebGL noise injection ✅
- Navi
